7 A few days later , the pedlar having moved on , two men appeared in the village inquiring who it was who had threatened to ill-treat and to murder an innocent pedlar .
8 They declared that the pedlar , in fear of his life , had complained to the king ; and that they had been sent to bring the lawless person who had said these things before the king himself .
9 Of course they soon found out about the donkey eating Nur Mahomed 's cabbages , and about the young man 's hot words ; but although the lad assured them that he had never said anything about murdering anyone , they replied they were ordered to arrest him , and bring him to take his trial before the king .
10 So , in spite of his protests , and the wails of his mother , he was carried off , and in due time brought before the king .
11 Of course Nur Mahomed never guessed that the supposed pedlar happened to have been the king himself , although nobody knew it .
12 But as he was very angry at what he had been told , he declared that he was going to make an example of this young man , and intended to teach him that even poor travelling pedlars could get justice in HIS country , and be protected from such lawlessness .
13 However , just as he was going to pronounce some very heavy sentence , there was a stir in the court , and up came Nur Mahomed 's old mother , weeping and lamenting , and begging to be heard .
14 The king ordered her to speak , and she began to plead for the boy , declaring how good he was , and how he was the support of her old age , and if he were put in prison she would die .
15 The king asked her who she was .
16 She replied that she was his mother .
17 ` His mother ? '
18 said the king ; ` you are too old , surely , to have so young a son ! '
19 Then the old woman , in her fright and distress , confessed the whole story of how she found the baby , and how she rescued and brought him up , and ended by beseeching the king for mercy .
20 It is easy to guess how , as the story came out , the king looked blacker and blacker , and more and more grim , until at last he was half fainting with rage and astonishment .
21 This , then , was the XXXXX he had left to die , after cruelly murdering his mother !	baby		Whereupon|age|baby|country|donkey|example|mother|sentence|son|tail

1 A neighbour passing by called out to him -- ` Hi !
2 I say !
3 why are you beating the pedlar 's donkey like that ? '
4 ` The pedlar should keep him from eating my cabbages , ' said Nur Mahomed ; ` if he comes this evening here again I 'll cut off his tail for him ! '
5 Whereupon he went off indoors , whistling cheerfully .
6 It happened that this neighbour was one of those people who make mischief by talking too much ; so , meeting the pedlar in the ` serai , ' or inn , that evening , he told him what had occurred , and added : ` Yes ; and the young spitfire said that if beating the donkey would not do , he would beat you also , and cut your nose off for a thief ! '
7 A few days later , the pedlar having moved on , two men appeared in the village inquiring who it was who had threatened to ill-treat and to murder an innocent pedlar .
8 They declared that the pedlar , in fear of his life , had complained to the king ; and that they had been sent to bring the lawless person who had said these things before the king himself .
9 Of course they soon found out about the donkey eating Nur Mahomed 's cabbages , and about the young man 's hot words ; but although the lad assured them that he had never said anything about murdering anyone , they replied they were ordered to arrest him , and bring him to take his trial before the king .
10 So , in spite of his protests , and the wails of his mother , he was carried off , and in due time brought before the king .
11 Of course Nur Mahomed never guessed that the supposed pedlar happened to have been the king himself , although nobody knew it .
12 But as he was very angry at what he had been told , he declared that he was going to make an example of this young man , and intended to teach him that even poor travelling pedlars could get justice in HIS country , and be protected from such lawlessness .
13 However , just as he was going to pronounce some very heavy sentence , there was a stir in the court , and up came Nur Mahomed 's old mother , weeping and lamenting , and begging to be heard .
14 The king ordered her to speak , and she began to plead for the boy , declaring how good he was , and how he was the support of her old age , and if he were put in prison she would die .
15 The king asked her who she was .
16 She replied that she was his mother .
17 ` His mother ? '
18 said the king ; ` you are too old , surely , to have so young a son ! '
19 Then the old woman , in her fright and distress , confessed the whole story of how she found the baby , and how she rescued and brought him up , and ended by beseeching the king for mercy .
20 It is easy to guess how , as the story came out , the king looked blacker and blacker , and more and more grim , until at last he was half fainting with rage and astonishment .

1 But as he was very angry at what he had been told , he declared that he was going to make an example of this young man , and intended to teach him that even poor travelling pedlars could get justice in HIS country , and be protected from such lawlessness .
2 However , just as he was going to pronounce some very heavy sentence , there was a stir in the court , and up came Nur Mahomed 's old mother , weeping and lamenting , and begging to be heard .
3 The king ordered her to speak , and she began to plead for the boy , declaring how good he was , and how he was the support of her old age , and if he were put in prison she would die .
4 The king asked her who she was .
5 She replied that she was his mother .
6 ` His mother ? '
7 said the king ; ` you are too old , surely , to have so young a son ! '
8 Then the old woman , in her fright and distress , confessed the whole story of how she found the baby , and how she rescued and brought him up , and ended by beseeching the king for mercy .
9 It is easy to guess how , as the story came out , the king looked blacker and blacker , and more and more grim , until at last he was half fainting with rage and astonishment .
10 This , then , was the baby he had left to die , after cruelly murdering his mother !
11 Surely fate might have spared him this !
12 He wished he had sufficient excuse to put the boy to death , for the old hermit 's prophecy came back to him as strongly as ever ; and yet the young man had done nothing bad enough to deserve such a punishment .
13 Everyone would call him a tyrant if he were to give such an order -- in fact , he dared not try it !
14 At length he collected himself enough to say : -- ` If this young man will enlist in my army I will let him off .
15 We have need of such as him , and a little discipline will do him good . '
16 Still the old woman pleaded that she could not live without her son , and was nearly as terrified at the idea of his becoming a soldier as she was at the thought of his being put in prison .
17 But at length the king -- determined to get the youth into his clutches -- pacified her by promising her a pension large enough to keep her in comfort ; and Nur Mahomed , to his own great delight , was duly enrolled in the king 's army .
18 As a soldier Nur Mahomed seemed to be in luck .
19 He was rather surprised , but much pleased , to find that he was always one of those chosen when any difficult or dangerous enterprise was afoot ; and , although he had the narrowest escapes on some occasions , still , the very desperateness of the situations in which he found himself gave him special chances of displaying his courage .
20 And as he was also modest and generous , he became a favourite with his officers and his comrades .
21 Thus it was not very surprising that , before very long , he became enrolled amongst the picked men of the XXXXX 's bodyguard .	king		army|astonishment|boy|delight|discipline|excuse|king|length|officers|woman

6 At length he collected himself enough to say : -- ` If this young man will enlist in my army I will let him off .
7 We have need of such as him , and a little discipline will do him good . '
8 Still the old woman pleaded that she could not live without her son , and was nearly as terrified at the idea of his becoming a soldier as she was at the thought of his being put in prison .
9 But at length the king -- determined to get the youth into his clutches -- pacified her by promising her a pension large enough to keep her in comfort ; and Nur Mahomed , to his own great delight , was duly enrolled in the king 's army .
10 As a soldier Nur Mahomed seemed to be in luck .
11 He was rather surprised , but much pleased , to find that he was always one of those chosen when any difficult or dangerous enterprise was afoot ; and , although he had the narrowest escapes on some occasions , still , the very desperateness of the situations in which he found himself gave him special chances of displaying his courage .
12 And as he was also modest and generous , he became a favourite with his officers and his comrades .
13 Thus it was not very surprising that , before very long , he became enrolled amongst the picked men of the king 's bodyguard .
14 The fact is , that the king had hoped to have got him killed in some fight or another ; but , seeing that , on the contrary , he throve on hard knocks , he was now determined to try more direct and desperate methods .
15 One day , soon after Nur Mahomed had entered the bodyguard , he was selected to be one of the soldiers told off to escort the king through the city .
16 The procession was marching on quite smoothly , when a man , armed with a dagger , rushed out of an alley straight towards the king .
17 Nur Mahomed , who was the nearest of the guards , threw himself in the way , and received the stab that had been apparently intended for the king .
18 Luckily the blow was a hurried one , and the dagger glanced on is breastbone , so that , although he received a severe wound , his youth and strength quickly got the better of it .
19 The king was , of course , obliged to take some notice of this brave deed , and as a reward made him one of his own attendants .
20 After this the strange adventures the young man passed through were endless .
21 Officers of the XXXXX were often sent on all sorts of secret and difficult errands , and such errands had a curious way of becoming necessary when Nur Mahomed was on duty .	bodyguard		attendants|bodyguard|course|excuse|king|man|officers|pension|situations|tyrant

20 He escaped somehow every time , and felt amused rather than anxious about the next adventure .

1 We have need of such as him , and a little discipline will do him good . '
2 Still the old woman pleaded that she could not live without her son , and was nearly as terrified at the idea of his becoming a soldier as she was at the thought of his being put in prison .
3 But at length the king -- determined to get the youth into his clutches -- pacified her by promising her a pension large enough to keep her in comfort ; and Nur Mahomed , to his own great delight , was duly enrolled in the king 's army .
4 As a soldier Nur Mahomed seemed to be in luck .
5 He was rather surprised , but much pleased , to find that he was always one of those chosen when any difficult or dangerous enterprise was afoot ; and , although he had the narrowest escapes on some occasions , still , the very desperateness of the situations in which he found himself gave him special chances of displaying his courage .
6 And as he was also modest and generous , he became a favourite with his officers and his comrades .
7 Thus it was not very surprising that , before very long , he became enrolled amongst the picked men of the king 's bodyguard .
8 The fact is , that the king had hoped to have got him killed in some fight or another ; but , seeing that , on the contrary , he throve on hard knocks , he was now determined to try more direct and desperate methods .
9 One day , soon after Nur Mahomed had entered the bodyguard , he was selected to be one of the soldiers told off to escort the king through the city .
10 The procession was marching on quite smoothly , when a man , armed with a dagger , rushed out of an alley straight towards the king .
11 Nur Mahomed , who was the nearest of the guards , threw himself in the way , and received the stab that had been apparently intended for the king .
12 Luckily the blow was a hurried one , and the dagger glanced on is breastbone , so that , although he received a severe wound , his youth and strength quickly got the better of it .
13 The king was , of course , obliged to take some notice of this brave deed , and as a reward made him one of his own attendants .
14 After this the strange adventures the young man passed through were endless .
15 Officers of the bodyguard were often sent on all sorts of secret and difficult errands , and such errands had a curious way of becoming necessary when Nur Mahomed was on duty .
16 Once , while he was taking a journey , a foot-bridge gave way under him ; once he was attacked by armed robbers ; a rock rolled down upon him in a mountain pass ; a heavy stone coping fell from a roof at his feet in a narrow city alley .
17 Altogether , Nur Mahomed began to think that , somewhere or other , he had made an enemy ; but he was light-hearted , and the thought did not much trouble him .
18 He escaped somehow every time , and felt amused rather than anxious about the next adventure .
19 It was the custom of that city that the officer for the day of the palace guards should receive all his food direct from the king 's kitchen .
20 One day , when Nur Mahomed 's turn came to be on duty , he was just sitting down to a delicious stew that had been sent in from the palace , when one of those gaunt , hungry dogs , which , in eastern countries , run about the streets , poked his nose in at the open guard-room door , and looked at Nur Mahomed with mouth watering and nostrils working .

1 He was rather surprised , but much pleased , to find that he was always one of those chosen when any difficult or dangerous enterprise was afoot ; and , although he had the narrowest escapes on some occasions , still , the very desperateness of the situations in which he found himself gave him special chances of displaying his courage .
2 And as he was also modest and generous , he became a favourite with his officers and his comrades .
3 Thus it was not very surprising that , before very long , he became enrolled amongst the picked men of the king 's bodyguard .
4 The fact is , that the king had hoped to have got him killed in some fight or another ; but , seeing that , on the contrary , he throve on hard knocks , he was now determined to try more direct and desperate methods .
5 One day , soon after Nur Mahomed had entered the bodyguard , he was selected to be one of the soldiers told off to escort the king through the city .
6 The procession was marching on quite smoothly , when a man , armed with a dagger , rushed out of an alley straight towards the king .
7 Nur Mahomed , who was the nearest of the guards , threw himself in the way , and received the stab that had been apparently intended for the king .
8 Luckily the blow was a hurried one , and the dagger glanced on is breastbone , so that , although he received a severe wound , his youth and strength quickly got the better of it .
9 The king was , of course , obliged to take some notice of this brave deed , and as a reward made him one of his own attendants .
10 After this the strange adventures the young man passed through were endless .
11 Officers of the bodyguard were often sent on all sorts of secret and difficult errands , and such errands had a curious way of becoming necessary when Nur Mahomed was on duty .
12 Once , while he was taking a journey , a foot-bridge gave way under him ; once he was attacked by armed robbers ; a rock rolled down upon him in a mountain pass ; a heavy stone coping fell from a roof at his feet in a narrow city alley .
13 Altogether , Nur Mahomed began to think that , somewhere or other , he had made an enemy ; but he was light-hearted , and the thought did not much trouble him .
14 He escaped somehow every time , and felt amused rather than anxious about the next adventure .
15 It was the custom of that city that the officer for the day of the palace guards should receive all his food direct from the king 's kitchen .
16 One day , when Nur Mahomed 's turn came to be on duty , he was just sitting down to a delicious stew that had been sent in from the palace , when one of those gaunt , hungry dogs , which , in eastern countries , run about the streets , poked his nose in at the open guard-room door , and looked at Nur Mahomed with mouth watering and nostrils working .
17 The kind-hearted young man picked out a lump of meat , went to the door , and threw it outside to him .
18 The dog pounced upon it , and gulped it down greedily , and was just turning to go , when it staggered , fell , rolled over , and died .
19 Nur Mahomed , who had been lazily watching him , stood still for a moment , then he came back whistling softly .
20 He gathered up the rest of his dinner and carefully wrapped it up to carry away and bury somewhere ; and then he sent back the empty plates .
21 How furious the XXXXX was when , at the next morning 's durbar , Nur Mahomed appeared before him fresh , alert and smiling as usual .	king		attendants|comrades|courage|deed|king|moment|procession|streets|time|wound

1 One day , soon after Nur Mahomed had entered the bodyguard , he was selected to be one of the soldiers told off to escort the king through the city .
2 The procession was marching on quite smoothly , when a man , armed with a dagger , rushed out of an alley straight towards the king .
3 Nur Mahomed , who was the nearest of the guards , threw himself in the way , and received the stab that had been apparently intended for the king .
4 Luckily the blow was a hurried one , and the dagger glanced on is breastbone , so that , although he received a severe wound , his youth and strength quickly got the better of it .
5 The king was , of course , obliged to take some notice of this brave deed , and as a reward made him one of his own attendants .
6 After this the strange adventures the young man passed through were endless .
7 Officers of the bodyguard were often sent on all sorts of secret and difficult errands , and such errands had a curious way of becoming necessary when Nur Mahomed was on duty .
8 Once , while he was taking a journey , a foot-bridge gave way under him ; once he was attacked by armed robbers ; a rock rolled down upon him in a mountain pass ; a heavy stone coping fell from a roof at his feet in a narrow city alley .
9 Altogether , Nur Mahomed began to think that , somewhere or other , he had made an enemy ; but he was light-hearted , and the thought did not much trouble him .
10 He escaped somehow every time , and felt amused rather than anxious about the next adventure .
11 It was the custom of that city that the officer for the day of the palace guards should receive all his food direct from the king 's kitchen .
12 One day , when Nur Mahomed 's turn came to be on duty , he was just sitting down to a delicious stew that had been sent in from the palace , when one of those gaunt , hungry dogs , which , in eastern countries , run about the streets , poked his nose in at the open guard-room door , and looked at Nur Mahomed with mouth watering and nostrils working .
13 The kind-hearted young man picked out a lump of meat , went to the door , and threw it outside to him .
14 The dog pounced upon it , and gulped it down greedily , and was just turning to go , when it staggered , fell , rolled over , and died .
15 Nur Mahomed , who had been lazily watching him , stood still for a moment , then he came back whistling softly .
16 He gathered up the rest of his dinner and carefully wrapped it up to carry away and bury somewhere ; and then he sent back the empty plates .
17 How furious the king was when , at the next morning 's durbar , Nur Mahomed appeared before him fresh , alert and smiling as usual .
18 He was determined , however , to try once more , and bidding the young man come into his presence that evening , gave orders that he was to carry a secret despatch to the governor of a distant province .
19 ` Make your preparations at once , ' added he , ` and be ready to start in the morning .
20 I myself will deliver you the papers at the last moment . '
21 Now this XXXXX was four or five days ' journey from the palace , and the governor of it was the most faithful servant the king had .	province		attendants|custom|journey|moment|notice|palace|province|rock|time|way

7 Officers of the bodyguard were often sent on all sorts of secret and difficult errands , and such errands had a curious way of becoming necessary when Nur Mahomed was on duty .
8 Once , while he was taking a journey , a foot-bridge gave way under him ; once he was attacked by armed robbers ; a rock rolled down upon him in a mountain pass ; a heavy stone coping fell from a roof at his feet in a narrow city alley .
9 Altogether , Nur Mahomed began to think that , somewhere or other , he had made an enemy ; but he was light-hearted , and the thought did not much trouble him .
10 He escaped somehow every time , and felt amused rather than anxious about the next adventure .
11 It was the custom of that city that the officer for the day of the palace guards should receive all his food direct from the king 's kitchen .
12 One day , when Nur Mahomed 's turn came to be on duty , he was just sitting down to a delicious stew that had been sent in from the palace , when one of those gaunt , hungry dogs , which , in eastern countries , run about the streets , poked his nose in at the open guard-room door , and looked at Nur Mahomed with mouth watering and nostrils working .
13 The kind-hearted young man picked out a lump of meat , went to the door , and threw it outside to him .
14 The dog pounced upon it , and gulped it down greedily , and was just turning to go , when it staggered , fell , rolled over , and died .
15 Nur Mahomed , who had been lazily watching him , stood still for a moment , then he came back whistling softly .
16 He gathered up the rest of his dinner and carefully wrapped it up to carry away and bury somewhere ; and then he sent back the empty plates .
17 How furious the king was when , at the next morning 's durbar , Nur Mahomed appeared before him fresh , alert and smiling as usual .
18 He was determined , however , to try once more , and bidding the young man come into his presence that evening , gave orders that he was to carry a secret despatch to the governor of a distant province .
19 ` Make your preparations at once , ' added he , ` and be ready to start in the morning .
20 I myself will deliver you the papers at the last moment . '
21 Now this province was four or five days ' journey from the XXXXX , and the governor of it was the most faithful servant the king had .	palace		Officers|attendants|countries|deed|enemy|orders|palace|rock|soldiers|thought

1 One day , soon after Nur Mahomed had entered the bodyguard , he was selected to be one of the soldiers told off to escort the king through the city .
2 The procession was marching on quite smoothly , when a man , armed with a dagger , rushed out of an alley straight towards the king .
3 Nur Mahomed , who was the nearest of the guards , threw himself in the way , and received the stab that had been apparently intended for the king .
4 Luckily the blow was a hurried one , and the dagger glanced on is breastbone , so that , although he received a severe wound , his youth and strength quickly got the better of it .
5 The king was , of course , obliged to take some notice of this brave deed , and as a reward made him one of his own attendants .
6 After this the strange adventures the young man passed through were endless .
7 Officers of the bodyguard were often sent on all sorts of secret and difficult errands , and such errands had a curious way of becoming necessary when Nur Mahomed was on duty .
8 Once , while he was taking a journey , a foot-bridge gave way under him ; once he was attacked by armed robbers ; a rock rolled down upon him in a mountain pass ; a heavy stone coping fell from a roof at his feet in a narrow city alley .
9 Altogether , Nur Mahomed began to think that , somewhere or other , he had made an enemy ; but he was light-hearted , and the thought did not much trouble him .
10 He escaped somehow every time , and felt amused rather than anxious about the next adventure .
11 It was the custom of that city that the officer for the day of the palace guards should receive all his food direct from the king 's kitchen .
12 One day , when Nur Mahomed 's turn came to be on duty , he was just sitting down to a delicious stew that had been sent in from the palace , when one of those gaunt , hungry dogs , which , in eastern countries , run about the streets , poked his nose in at the open guard-room door , and looked at Nur Mahomed with mouth watering and nostrils working .
13 The kind-hearted young man picked out a lump of meat , went to the door , and threw it outside to him .
14 The dog pounced upon it , and gulped it down greedily , and was just turning to go , when it staggered , fell , rolled over , and died .
15 Nur Mahomed , who had been lazily watching him , stood still for a moment , then he came back whistling softly .

14 He was determined , however , to try once more , and bidding the young man come into his presence that evening , gave orders that he was to carry a secret despatch to the governor of a distant province .
15 ` Make your preparations at once , ' added he , ` and be ready to start in the morning .
16 I myself will deliver you the papers at the last moment . '
17 Now this province was four or five days ' journey from the palace , and the governor of it was the most faithful servant the king had .
18 He could be silent as the grave , and prided himself on his obedience .
19 Whilst he was an old and tried servant of the king 's , his wife had been almost a mother to the young princess ever since the queen had died some years before .
20 It happened that , a little before this time , the princess had been sent away for her health to another remote province ; and whilst she was there her old friend , the governor 's wife , had begged her to come and stay with them as soon as she could .
21 The XXXXX accepted gladly , and was actually staying in the governor 's house at the very time when the king made up his mind to send Nur Mahomed there with the mysterious despatch .	princess		attendants|bodyguard|day|deed|duty|journey|orders|princess|robbers|stew

1 The king was , of course , obliged to take some notice of this brave deed , and as a reward made him one of his own attendants .
2 After this the strange adventures the young man passed through were endless .
3 Officers of the bodyguard were often sent on all sorts of secret and difficult errands , and such errands had a curious way of becoming necessary when Nur Mahomed was on duty .
4 Once , while he was taking a journey , a foot-bridge gave way under him ; once he was attacked by armed robbers ; a rock rolled down upon him in a mountain pass ; a heavy stone coping fell from a roof at his feet in a narrow city alley .
5 Altogether , Nur Mahomed began to think that , somewhere or other , he had made an enemy ; but he was light-hearted , and the thought did not much trouble him .
6 He escaped somehow every time , and felt amused rather than anxious about the next adventure .
7 It was the custom of that city that the officer for the day of the palace guards should receive all his food direct from the king 's kitchen .
8 One day , when Nur Mahomed 's turn came to be on duty , he was just sitting down to a delicious stew that had been sent in from the palace , when one of those gaunt , hungry dogs , which , in eastern countries , run about the streets , poked his nose in at the open guard-room door , and looked at Nur Mahomed with mouth watering and nostrils working .
9 The kind-hearted young man picked out a lump of meat , went to the door , and threw it outside to him .
10 The dog pounced upon it , and gulped it down greedily , and was just turning to go , when it staggered , fell , rolled over , and died .
11 Nur Mahomed , who had been lazily watching him , stood still for a moment , then he came back whistling softly .
12 He gathered up the rest of his dinner and carefully wrapped it up to carry away and bury somewhere ; and then he sent back the empty plates .
13 How furious the king was when , at the next morning 's durbar , Nur Mahomed appeared before him fresh , alert and smiling as usual .
14 He was determined , however , to try once more , and bidding the young man come into his presence that evening , gave orders that he was to carry a secret despatch to the governor of a distant province .
15 ` Make your preparations at once , ' added he , ` and be ready to start in the morning .
16 I myself will deliver you the papers at the last moment . '
17 Now this province was four or five days ' journey from the palace , and the governor of it was the most faithful servant the king had .
18 He could be silent as the grave , and prided himself on his obedience .
19 Whilst he was an old and tried servant of the king 's , his wife had been almost a mother to the young princess ever since the queen had died some years before .
20 It happened that , a little before this time , the princess had been sent away for her health to another remote province ; and whilst she was there her old friend , the governor 's wife , had begged her to come and stay with them as soon as she could .

20 At length he reached the castle gates , and was at once admitted , as he was in the uniform of the king 's bodyguard .

10 Whilst he was an old and tried servant of the king 's , his wife had been almost a mother to the young princess ever since the queen had died some years before .
11 It happened that , a little before this time , the princess had been sent away for her health to another remote province ; and whilst she was there her old friend , the governor 's wife , had begged her to come and stay with them as soon as she could .

13 According to orders Nur Mahomed presented himself early the next morning at the king 's private apartments .
14 His best horse was saddled , food placed in is saddle-bag , and with some money tied up in his waist-band , he was ready to start .

17 The weather was very hot ; but Nur Mahomed thought that the sooner his precious letter was delivered the better ; so that , by dint of riding most of each night and resting only in the hottest part of the day , he found himself , by noon on the third day , approaching the town which was his final destination .
18 Not a soul was to be seen anywhere ; and Nur Mahomed , stiff , dry , thirsty , and tired , looked longingly over the wall into the gardens , and marked the fountains , the green grass , the shady apricot orchards , and giant mulberry trees , and wished he were there .
19 At length he reached the castle gates , and was at once admitted , as he was in the uniform of the king 's bodyguard .
20 The governor was resting , the soldier said , and could not see him until the evening .
21 So Nur Mahomed handed over his XXXXX to an attendant , and wandered down into the lovely gardens he had seen from the road , and sat down in the shade to rest himself .	horse		grave|health|horse|letter|moment|noon|orders|palace|time|wife

1 The dog pounced upon it , and gulped it down greedily , and was just turning to go , when it staggered , fell , rolled over , and died .
2 Nur Mahomed , who had been lazily watching him , stood still for a moment , then he came back whistling softly .
3 He gathered up the rest of his dinner and carefully wrapped it up to carry away and bury somewhere ; and then he sent back the empty plates .
4 How furious the king was when , at the next morning 's durbar , Nur Mahomed appeared before him fresh , alert and smiling as usual .
5 He was determined , however , to try once more , and bidding the young man come into his presence that evening , gave orders that he was to carry a secret despatch to the governor of a distant province .
6 ` Make your preparations at once , ' added he , ` and be ready to start in the morning .
7 I myself will deliver you the papers at the last moment . '
8 Now this province was four or five days ' journey from the palace , and the governor of it was the most faithful servant the king had .
9 He could be silent as the grave , and prided himself on his obedience .
10 Whilst he was an old and tried servant of the king 's , his wife had been almost a mother to the young princess ever since the queen had died some years before .
11 It happened that , a little before this time , the princess had been sent away for her health to another remote province ; and whilst she was there her old friend , the governor 's wife , had begged her to come and stay with them as soon as she could .
12 The princess accepted gladly , and was actually staying in the governor 's house at the very time when the king made up his mind to send Nur Mahomed there with the mysterious despatch .
13 According to orders Nur Mahomed presented himself early the next morning at the king 's private apartments .
14 His best horse was saddled , food placed in is saddle-bag , and with some money tied up in his waist-band , he was ready to start .
15 The king handed over to him a sealed packet , desiring him to give it himself only into the hands of the governor , and to no one else .
16 Nur Mahomed hid it carefully in his turban , swung himself into the saddle , and five minutes later rode out of the city gates , and set out on his long journey .
17 The weather was very hot ; but Nur Mahomed thought that the sooner his precious letter was delivered the better ; so that , by dint of riding most of each night and resting only in the hottest part of the day , he found himself , by noon on the third day , approaching the town which was his final destination .
18 Not a soul was to be seen anywhere ; and Nur Mahomed , stiff , dry , thirsty , and tired , looked longingly over the wall into the gardens , and marked the fountains , the green grass , the shady apricot orchards , and giant mulberry trees , and wished he were there .
19 At length he reached the castle gates , and was at once admitted , as he was in the uniform of the king 's bodyguard .
20 The governor was resting , the soldier said , and could not see him until the evening .

16 The governor was resting , the soldier said , and could not see him until the evening .
17 So Nur Mahomed handed over his horse to an attendant , and wandered down into the lovely gardens he had seen from the road , and sat down in the shade to rest himself .
18 He flung himself on his back and watched the birds twittering and chattering in the trees above him .
19 Through the branches he could see great patches of sky where the kites wheeled and circled incessantly , with shrill whistling cried .
20 Bees buzzed over the flowers with a soothing sound , and in a few minutes Nur Mahomed was fast asleep .
21 Every day , through the heat of the afternoon , the XXXXX , and his wife also , used to lie down for two or three hours in their own rooms , and so , for the matter of that , did most people in the palace .	governor		destination|food|friend|governor|journey|moment|road|town|turban|wall
